<div id="review_2351824038" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2351824038" />
    <a title="Henk" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/76202320-henk"><img alt="Henk" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557871304p2/76202320.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2351824038?book_show_action=true">Jul 31, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Henk" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Henk" href="/user/show/76202320-henk">Henk</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9789025308636" href="/book/show/38720055-het-hoofdkussenboek">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/76202320-henk?shelf=japanese-literature">japanese-literature</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2351824038" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10578916951279197408"><i>‚ÄúEverything that cries at night I find splendid, except for baby‚Äôs‚Äù</i> - Sei Sonagon<br/><br/>This thousand year old book has a lot of still very relatable observations besides the one above. Sonagon also does not like people who are to assertive, certain coloured clothing, the embarrassment that comes from talking behind someones back (and that person actually overhearing) and off course: mosquitos. <br/><br/>The Pillowbook is kind of a diary, with decadent snippets of imperial court life intertwined with lists with </span>
  <span id="freeText10578916951279197408" style="display:none"><i>‚ÄúEverything that cries at night I find splendid, except for baby‚Äôs‚Äù</i> - Sei Sonagon<br /><br />This thousand year old book has a lot of still very relatable observations besides the one above. Sonagon also does not like people who are to assertive, certain coloured clothing, the embarrassment that comes from talking behind someones back (and that person actually overhearing) and off course: mosquitos. <br /><br />The Pillowbook is kind of a diary, with decadent snippets of imperial court life intertwined with lists with do‚Äôs and don‚Äôts, which reminded me a lot of current day lifestyle magazines (for instance the author reminds us on what lakes to visit and what colours fit certain seasons). Also sometimes things get a bit more juicy or snappish and its like your reading an ancient and literary version of Sex and the City. All this makes the book an interesting and remarkable easy read for a modern day reader, even though there is not really a coherent story, character development or an apotheosis. <br />The way how she captures moments before they are gone forever, which is especially poignant because this Dutch translation is very carefully and lovingly annotated, giving much context on the historical events, including the fact that the empress Sonagan serves fell from grace and died quite young, is excellent.<br /><br />What is overly apparent in the world of the medieval Japanese Imperial court is that people have too much time at hand. Court ceremonies, nightly encounters with lovers, Buddhist temple visits and lots of moving about between various palaces fill the days and years of Sonagon and her peers. Poetry is used as a hidden language and comes back seemingly in every conversation. Everyone is looking to recite an appropriate poem for the circumstances at hand, be it in written or oral responses. The only modern day equivalent I could think of is how people on sites like Tumblr use internet memes, while I also had associations with Victorian plant language. It gives an impression of a live not spend outside in the world but only known through books, which is probably correct given that women were often times hidden behind blinds or stately curtains even in the court itself.<br /><br />Sonagon as a person is not very clearly pictured from her Pillowbook. Is she really a favourite of the empress and as witty and literary skilled as she tries to come across? Or are the sections in the end more true, where she is corrected by the empress for using the word ‚Äúunbearable‚Äù in a response and where she sends of a commoner, whose house and livelihood burnt down due to sparks from the palace, cruelly away with a poem as only compensation, closer to the true Sonagon? In her defence, at times she does come across as very frank, for instance by admitting that she feels a pang of joy when something bad happens to someone she loathes and how nice it is to sometimes gossip. But in the end she does strike me as a lady who likes to portray herself in a positive manner, talking to us as readers in a way not unlike some modern day aunts during a dinner party with the rest of the family would do.<br /><br />Overall an interesting read, especially since I am fond of Japanese culture, and enough to ponder about, without even the burden to seek a fitting poem for capturing the whole experience of reading the Pillowbook. 3,5 stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10578916951279197408" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_21508951" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/21508951" />
    <a title="Julie Ruble" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/65647-julie-ruble"><img alt="Julie Ruble" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1199461959p2/65647.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/21508951?book_show_action=true">May 03, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Julie Ruble" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Julie Ruble" href="/user/show/65647-julie-ruble">Julie Ruble</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer21508951" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4198164963079000572">I haven't finished this book yet, but have read a lot of it. I skip over some of the daily accounts in favor of the lists / observations / character sketches. I need to go back and fill in the blanks, but it might be awhile before I get to it. For now:<br/><br/>A "pillow book" is a collection of random notes, character sketches, lists, poems, and observations that the Japanese upper class during the Heian period might have kept in the drawers of their wooden pillows. Having an example of the pillow book g</span>
  <span id="freeText4198164963079000572" style="display:none">I haven't finished this book yet, but have read a lot of it. I skip over some of the daily accounts in favor of the lists / observations / character sketches. I need to go back and fill in the blanks, but it might be awhile before I get to it. For now:<br /><br />A "pillow book" is a collection of random notes, character sketches, lists, poems, and observations that the Japanese upper class during the Heian period might have kept in the drawers of their wooden pillows. Having an example of the pillow book genre is so intriguing! It's a great snapshot of the life and attitude of the Japanese upper class at the time.<br /><br />There's tension in this pillow book because Shonagon claims she wants to keep her thoughts private while clearly writing for an outside audience. And oh, what colorful thoughts she has! <br /><br />Sei is arrogant, privileged, and oblivious or offensive to people she calls "completely insignificant" (think servants, common people, even lowly priests). At one point she mocks a man whose house has burned down by giving him what appears to be an alms slip -- he cannot read, so he thinks she has given him charity -- with a hateful poem written on it instead of alms. The fact that she writes this account in her (widely-read) pillow book and describes it with great mirth suggests that her attitude was common and acceptable among ladies of her rank.<br /><br />Despite her obvious flaws, Sei appreciates beauty and sympathy (okay, apparently only for the upper class) and humor. I was very surprised by the humorous, playful, confident tone in this text. If someone had mentioned a Japanese woman's diary from the year 900 to me, I'd have assumed it was dry and boring. Not so at all! For the history, Sei's colorful personality, and the fascinating genre of the pillow book itself, this text gets 4 stars. </span>
  <a data-text-id="4198164963079000572" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3161871141" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3161871141" />
    <a title="Paul" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/68029956-paul"><img alt="Paul" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1552062265p2/68029956.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3161871141?book_show_action=true">Jan 26, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Paul" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Paul" href="/user/show/68029956-paul">Paul</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780140448061" href="/book/show/18187.The_Pillow_Book">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68029956-paul?shelf=5-stars">5-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68029956-paul?shelf=completed-2020">completed-2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68029956-paul?shelf=cpl">cpl</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68029956-paul?shelf=non-art-photo">non-art-photo</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68029956-paul?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68029956-paul?shelf=poetry-east">poetry-east</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68029956-paul?shelf=poetry">poetry</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3161871141" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4111343147850795564">Sooooooooo good. This was one of the last books on my to-read list of classical Japanese prose/poetry, and I figured it would be a tedious non-fiction companion to Shikibu's <i>Tale of Genji</i>, but I guess I'm in the minority insofar as I think <i>Genji</i> is both overrated and overlong, while the <i>Pillow Book</i> is not the shallow court gossip that I'd been expecting, but rather a charmingly artful and exquisite collection of <i>belles lettres</i>. <br/><br/>I was immediately reminded of the diary of Samuel Pepys -- both high</span>
  <span id="freeText4111343147850795564" style="display:none">Sooooooooo good. This was one of the last books on my to-read list of classical Japanese prose/poetry, and I figured it would be a tedious non-fiction companion to Shikibu's <i>Tale of Genji</i>, but I guess I'm in the minority insofar as I think <i>Genji</i> is both overrated and overlong, while the <i>Pillow Book</i> is not the shallow court gossip that I'd been expecting, but rather a charmingly artful and exquisite collection of <i>belles lettres</i>. <br /><br />I was immediately reminded of the diary of Samuel Pepys -- both high-ranking functionaries in the royal court, the same sense of immediacy, of daily life, the humor, the deft characterization and descriptions, etc., though Sh≈çnagon is definitely a better writer, with more refined (some might say overrefined!) taste. The word "Proustian" is almost certainly used too often, but her languid descriptions of flowers, romantic love, aristocratic society, etc., as well as her sensitivity to social gradations and niceties (if not her prose style) constantly reminded me of Proust, in a good way. <br /><br />Probably the most surreal moment, for me, was where she was writing about all the ponds she had visited -- yes, it sounds boring but holy crap, her lists of random things are so compelling -- and halfway through she writes: "Saruwasa Pond is a very special place, because the Emperor paid it a formal visit when he heard how one of the Palace Maidens had drowned herself there." I immediately thought of one of Hitomaro's most famous (and beautiful) poems on a similar topic, and then literally jumped up in my chair a little bit when I saw her next line: "Thinking of Hitomaro's marvelous words 'her hair tangled in sleep,' there's really nothing I can add" (?!), as I suddenly realized that, of course, a Japanese lady-in-waiting in 1002 A.D. would naturally <i>also</i> be a big fan of Hitomaro, lol.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4111343147850795564" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_317994199" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/317994199" />
    <a title="Hal O&#39;Brien" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2797330-hal-o-brien"><img alt="Hal O&#39;Brien" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1268723731p2/2797330.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/317994199?book_show_action=true">Apr 24, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hal O&#39;Brien" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hal O&#39;Brien" href="/user/show/2797330-hal-o-brien">Hal O&#39;Brien</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2797330-hal-o-brien?shelf=essays">essays</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2797330-hal-o-brien?shelf=asia-japan">asia-japan</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2797330-hal-o-brien?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer317994199" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18237922431877678019">Written at the turn of the 10th Century CE, Shonagon is easily the first blogger. Lists, streams of consciousness, the minutiae of everyday life, insights on the larger culture of the Heian period of Japan... It's all here. The West wouldn't see anything like it until Montaigne and Pepys.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1627687762" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1627687762" />
    <a title="shanghao" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8606081-shanghao"><img alt="shanghao" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1579963873p2/8606081.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1627687762?book_show_action=true">May 03, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="shanghao" class="user" itemprop="url" name="shanghao" href="/user/show/8606081-shanghao">shanghao</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8606081-shanghao?shelf=orient">orient</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8606081-shanghao?shelf=ye-olde-days">ye-olde-days</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8606081-shanghao?shelf=shorts">shorts</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8606081-shanghao?shelf=society">society</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1627687762" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5694002350203996260"><b>Beautiful Things</b><br/>Flashes of wit, impunity, tenderness. Contradictions and multiple facets of Sei's character. Unabashed honesty, pettiness and surprising piety. <br/><br/><b>Annoying Things</b><br/>Intrusions to the actual entries from the translator, which usually ended as abruptly as they started. <br/><br/>The explanations were helpful, but the inconsistent way in which things were explained (some via footnotes, some directly slipped between the paragraphs) can be confusing. Definitely affected my enjoyment of reading this, </span>
  <span id="freeText5694002350203996260" style="display:none"><b>Beautiful Things</b><br />Flashes of wit, impunity, tenderness. Contradictions and multiple facets of Sei's character. Unabashed honesty, pettiness and surprising piety. <br /><br /><b>Annoying Things</b><br />Intrusions to the actual entries from the translator, which usually ended as abruptly as they started. <br /><br />The explanations were helpful, but the inconsistent way in which things were explained (some via footnotes, some directly slipped between the paragraphs) can be confusing. Definitely affected my enjoyment of reading this, therefore the 2 stars. I'm inclined to rate the content 4 stars actually.<br /><br /><b>Things to Ponder</b><br />How the most famous literature of this era had come from women rather than men, as opposed to China. Apparently this was attributed to the men usually trying to emulate the great Chinese poets, whereas the women were less restrained by norms and as a result produced more authentic, lasting works.<br /><br /><b>The Value of Triviality</b><br />Sei Shonagon fussed over the most trivial things, and perhaps she could be seen as shallow and aloof to the greater issues of the world. Hers might only have been a reflection of idyllic court life, and there might have been real suffering beyond the palace. <br /><br />Yet, I felt that what she's experiencing and her 'first-world complaints', so to speak, are bygone rarities that we in this current shambolic era do not have the luxury to express as nonchalantly as she did. <br /><br />We should be so lucky when our most pressing concerns consist of pretending to be asleep, to no avail, when someone you're not in the mood of seeing come a-knocking in the wee small hours of the morning, the nerve! <br /><br />Frankly I'm not sure which is better, living in trying times but developing a more wordly and magnanimous heart, with many suffering the consequences of dire decisions; or in an idyllic one where one is more self-centred, but the general populace happier on the whole in a simpler, small-minded world if you will. <br /><br />Well if anything, change will come. As Sei Shonagon's trivial but relatively peaceful era had passed, so will our erratic, exciting(?) one give way. <br /><br />When change does sweep through our current times, may it be for peace and joy. (gosh I sound like a beauty pageant contestant. But really.) I sure hope the complaints in my no-holds-barred pillow book would only be trivial, petty ones - not because I'm shallow (though I am a lot of the time ^^), but because it's afforded by a life and world well worth living.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5694002350203996260" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_28366904" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/28366904" />
    <a title="Scott" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/40533-scott"><img alt="Scott" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1271013583p2/40533.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/28366904?book_show_action=true">Jul 26, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Scott" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Scott" href="/user/show/40533-scott">Scott</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer28366904" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer144528120563037935">Very fun way to get to know Heian Japanese culture if you don't already.<br/><br/>If you do, then Sh≈çnagon is opinionated and contrary enough that she can really make the world come alive. Her opinions don't always match up to the popular ones at the time, and it's neat to start to recognize when that happens without referring to the endnotes.<br/><br/>The Ivan Morris translation is fully half appendices and notes, which really help in understanding what's going on and what everything means, but they're also skippa</span>
  <span id="freeText144528120563037935" style="display:none">Very fun way to get to know Heian Japanese culture if you don't already.<br /><br />If you do, then Sh≈çnagon is opinionated and contrary enough that she can really make the world come alive. Her opinions don't always match up to the popular ones at the time, and it's neat to start to recognize when that happens without referring to the endnotes.<br /><br />The Ivan Morris translation is fully half appendices and notes, which really help in understanding what's going on and what everything means, but they're also skippable if you're not into doing a real deep reading. I only flipped to the end notes about a third of the time, but I was usually happy with what I learned that way.<br /><br />I also enjoy this translation more than the parts of a different one I read a few years back. I felt the other one over-Westernized it, which is dangerous when much of this writing, not to mention the lifestyle, is based on subtlety and wordplay. <br /><br />Anyway, recommended if you've got any interest in this period of history.</span>
  <a data-text-id="144528120563037935" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16652983-eadweard?shelf=favorites-or-really-liked">favorites-or-really-liked</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer530459803" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3635897230444162624">This was very enjoyable to read, just pick it up and read a few entries a day, then read a few more the next day, there's no plot or anything to keep in mind. It's great being able to read something like this, what amused this woman, what she hated, what was happening at the court, which events she attended, lists of things she likes and dislikes, the whole book is like this, anecdotes, events and lists.<br/><br/>"Everything that cries in the night is wonderfull. With the exception of babies."</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_1171904162" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1171904162" />
    <a title="Bob" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2432880-bob"><img alt="Bob" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1245441460p2/2432880.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1171904162?book_show_action=true">Jan 17, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bob" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bob" href="/user/show/2432880-bob">Bob</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2432880-bob?shelf=asia">asia</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1171904162" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10522612277921815582"> The element of <i>The Tale of Genji</i> which appealed most to me was its exoticism, which <i>The Pillow Book</i>, or at least these extracts, captures without any of the effort of following the former's plot echoes, characterization, and psychological nuances. Sei Shonagon can't capture Murasaki's deep sense of the tragic evanescence of life, but the lack only makes her more appealing, in some ways, to a modern reader. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('GX/GmYom4Dco1G3aQWL7PCZRpa6wSSIDL4+P/s0XORBPL8V8+PHrDA/IRETFykmBLV5uxhCxyPXMfXzOafZazw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('uo3S6rNeshG3v9erZCTBUGJ8jEH4SJVBexwiep7XnePs3dEPwYm5KpCj/jXgjHPtaXNHKViwf7eY7tFKOjb+PA==')})
  }

Too impetuous to be satisfied as a subsidiary wife, this beautiful (and unnamed) noblewoman of the Heian dynasty protests the marriage system of her time in one of Japanese literature\'s earliest attempts to portray difficult elements of the predominant social hierarchy. A classic work of early Japanese prose, The Gossamer Years is an important example of the development of Heian literature, which, at its best, represents an extraordinary flowering of realistic expression, an attempt, unique for its age, to treat the human condition with frankness and honesty. A timeless and intimate glimpse into the culture of ancient Japan, this translation by Edward Seidensticker paints a revealing picture of married life in the Heian period.<\/span>\n  <a As Emperor Go-Daigo fended off a challenge from the usurping Hojo family, and Japan stood at the brink of a dark political era, Kenk≈ç held fast to his Buddhist beliefs and took refuge in the pleasures of solitude. Written between 1330 and 1332, Essays in Idleness reflects the congenial priest\'s thoughts on a variety of subjects. His brief writings, some no more than a few sentences long and ranging in focus from politics and ethics to nature and mythology, mark the crystallization of a distinct Japanese principle: that beauty is to be celebrated, though it will ultimately perish. Through his appreciation of the world around him and his keen understanding of historical events, Kenk≈ç conveys the essence of Buddhist philosophy and its subtle teachings for all readers. Insisting on the uncertainty of this world, Kenk≈ç asks that we waste no time in following the way of Buddha.\n\nIn this fresh edition, Donald Keene\'s critically acclaimed translation is joined by a The result was an autobiographical narrative, a tale of thirty-six years (1271-1306) in the life of Lady Nijo, starting when she became the concubine of a retired emperor in Kyoto at the age of fourteen and ending, several love affairs later, with an account of her new life as a wandering Buddhist nun.Through the vagaries of history, however, the glory of Lady Nijo\'s story has taken six and half centuries to arrive. The Confessions of Lady Nijo or Towazugatari in Japanese, was not widely circulated after it was written, perhaps because of the dynastic quarrel that soon split the imperial family, or perhaps because of Lady Nijo\'s intimate portrait of a very human emperor. Whatever the cause, the book was neglected, then forgotten completely, and only a single manuscript survived. This was finally discovered in 1940, but would not be published until after World War II in 1950.
